            "Presenter": "David H. Turpin, President and Chair of General Faculties Council; Steven Dew, Provost and Vice-President (Academic) ",
            "Description": "Purpose of the Proposal: To obtain feedback on the Vision, Mission and Values document, which will be used in the creation of the first draft of the new institutional strategic plan. Discussion: The Chair reported that over 400 pages of material had been gathered through meetings, round tables, forums, and online contributions; however, there had been limited feedback on the University’s vision, mission and values statement, which are integral elements of the institution’s mandate. In the discussion that followed, it was suggested that the wording was adequate but could be strengthened and made more concise. A member suggested that the University of Alberta’s unique delivery of a bilingual and multicultural educational experience should be emphasized within the statements, and that students are requesting specific changes to the language in this regard. A member noted that the language used within the “Pride” section could be amended. A member offered concluding remarks that although the existing and proposed statements are adequate, that there are remaining gaps, and she encouraged a deeper look into them. The Chair thanked members for their suggestions, and pointed out that there are still opportunities to provide feedback, in person and online.",

            "Item No.": "5",
            "Agenda Title": "Academic Governance at the University of Alberta",
            "Motion": "I. THAT the General Faculties Council will review the delegation of its authorities to all of its current committees, and by 30 June 2016 vote on whether to renew or revise these delegated authorities.; II. THAT the review of the governance and operations of the General Faculties Council is to be informed by the June 2013 report \"A Reflection on the State of Academic Governance at the University of Alberta.\"",
            "Action Requested": "Discussion/Advice",
            "Date": "2016-01-25",
            "Committee": "GFC",
            "Proposed By": "David Turpin, President and Chair, General Faculties Council",
            "Presenter": "David Turpin, President and Chair, General Faculties Council",
            "Description": "Purpose of the Proposal: To frame the initial discussion of the revitalization of academic governance and establish next steps in the process of considering recent reports and discussion papers on GFC reforms. Discussion: The Chair noted that collegial governance involves many individuals participating in the decision-making process and that the current GFC has been shaped by decisions made by its members over time. He added that GFC will continue to change in response to the decisions made by the current membership. The Chair referred the members to the package developed by GFC Executive Committee to frame the discussion on academic governance at the University of Alberta. He further noted that the two Motions added to the agenda relate to this important issue and would be considered with this item. A member noted that this is an important and timely discussion. Members commented on a number of items: one member suggested the GFC should consider mandatory attendance to ensure that the diverse views of all Faculties are represented; another member suggested that the day and time of GFC meeting should be re-visited as a Tuesday or Thursday slot might work better for student attendance. A member noted that the information about academic governance on the University Governance website was difficult to understand. A member noted that Council on Student Affairs (COSA), a body under GFC within the Post-Secondary Learning Act (PSLA), was going be reviewed in terms of mandate, structure and scope. Members discussed the importance of communication, suggesting that improving the flow of information from GFC and its Standing Committees should be a priority. A member noted that GFC may be hindered legislatively by the Post-Secondary Learning Act (PSLA), indicating that the Board of Governors retains a lot of unilateral authority over matters at the University. The member further noted that there has been discussion surrounding this balance of power among other western Canadian universities recently. The Chair, in response, pointed out that GFC graduate student member Mr Brayden Whitlock had recently published an article on this issue entitled, “Who Watches Academic Watch Dogs?” The Chair stated that the University of Alberta’s GFC is twice the size of the average academic senate, which may have an impact on how decisions are made and invited members to discuss GFC’s delegations. Members expressed concern that the delegation of authority meant that important items were not reaching the floor of GFC and that GFC was just rubber stamping decisions. Members agreed that committee delegations should reviewed on a regular basis. It was noted by a member that, when delegations are made, the full implications may not be realized. One member expressed his struggle with the mandate of GFC Executive to consider urgent matters on behalf of GFC. Regarding committees, a member pointed out the value of having smaller, more specialized bodies to consider proposals in detail and noted that standing committees consider very technical things which, in concert with member composition, provide a very high-quality service to GFC. A member suggested that standing committees should realize when strategic items should be brought forward to GFC. A member cautioned that de-delegation could overload GFC with a lot of minor business, such as course and program changes. A member noted that the issue may be how to get GFC involved in meaningful initiatives and suggested GFC engage in a discussion of principles. Another member indicated that GFC should be involved in the discussion of critical issues and that a cultural change may be required to foster this. The Chair of the GFC Nominating Committee, Dr van der Baan, noted that the committee uses a summary document of each GFC Standing Committee’s Terms of Reference, which members have found useful. He also reminded members that a new replenishment cycle has begun should members choose to serve on a standing committee. A member suggested that the standing committees could be asked to provide GFC with an annual report of activities undertaken with delegated authority from GFC. Another member noted that the standing committees have started regularly reporting to GFC on activities. It was also noted that minutes and meeting materials are available online at the governance website. A member suggested that members of GFC could be notified when agendas for all upcoming GFC standing committee meetings were available online. The Chair suggested that the process could begin with a review of GFC’s delegations, and he invited the University Secretary to comment. Ms Haggarty-France noted that in addition to GFC’s delegated authority to its Standing Committees, there is delegated authority from the Board of Governors, within the University of Alberta Policies and Procedures Online (UAPPOL), to individuals, and to other units such as Faculty Councils.; A member indicated her strong support for using the Students’ Union Report as the basis for the future changes to academic governance, citing the specificity in the document, such as improvements to minutes and receiving advice. There was a discussion on what was meant by the term “guided by” in the Motion. A member of GFC indicated that this meant to indicate that the document will be considered. He further noted that this document was selected because it specifically mentions discussions, reporting and a commitment towards the notion of collegial governance and informed decision-making. The Chair clarified that if the Motion is carried, GFC is not held to all of the recommendations within the Report. The mover and seconder agreed to the friendly amendment to say “informed by” instead of “guided by”. The Chair stated that the GFC Executive Committee would review this issue in greater detail and report back to GFC with a plan. He also noted the possibility of scheduling an additional meeting of GFC in this academic year for further discussion.",

            "Item No.": "8",
            "Agenda Title": "Report on Evaluation of Online Universal Student Ratings of Instruction (USRI) ",
            "Motion": "N/A ",
            "Action Requested": "Discussion/Advice, Information",
            "Date": "2016-01-25",
            "Committee": "GFC",
            "Proposed By": "Mike MacGregor, Vice-Provost and Associate Vice-President of Information Technology; Scott Delinger, Director, Research Computing",
            "Presenter": "Scott Delinger, Director, Research Computing, Information Services & Technology; Sarah Forgie, Vice-Provost (Learning Initiatives) and Chair of GFC Committee on the Learning Environment",
            "Description": "Purpose of the Proposal: To report on the effects on USRIs due to the transition from paper to electronic means. During the transition, a final report was noted as a necessary summary of what effects were seen. Discussion: Dr Forgie and Dr Delinger summarized the findings of the report evaluating the move to online Universal Students Ratings of Instruction (USRIs) at the University of Alberta. They reported that the transition of the USRI from paper format to electronic means has resulted in a drop in average response rates, but noted that median scores remained the same with lab sections experiencing a greater decrease in response rates compared to lecture sections. Dr Delinger noted that this is consistent with the experience of other institutions that have made the transition to electronic USRI tools. Dr Forgie noted that the data would continue to be monitored. During the ensuing discussion, members expressed several comments and questions surrounding how much money this initiative has saved the institution; whether the data could include the race and gender of the instructor; an update in regards to written comments; and USRI usage for courses with ten students or less.",

            "Description": "Purpose of the Proposal: The Helping Individuals at Risk Policy (HIAR) was introduced and an intake function was created to work in conjunction with the Office of Safe Disclosure and Human Rights (SDHR). The policy requires that annual reporting to General Faculties Council (GFC) and to the Board of Governors will occur after each year of operation. The purpose of this report is to provide an overview of the activities of each office and to comment on trends and issues in these. Discussion: Ms Persson and Mr Wade King provided members with a summary of the annual report of the Helping Individuals at Risk and Safe Disclosure and Human Rights for 2014-15, noting that the Office of Safe Disclosure and Human Rights (OSDHR) provided intake and referral for 79 formal disclosures, reflecting an increase of disclosures from academic staff and students and a decrease of disclosures from non- academic staff. Ms Persson added that the most frequently disclosed matters continue to be discrimination and harassment, but OSDHR received report of numerous other issues including safety, fraud and the application of collective agreements. Ms Persson also provided members with a summary of OSDHR educational activities undertaken within the community during the reporting period.",

Next meeting date: Monday, March 21, 2016  \nDocumentation was before members unless otherwise noted. \nMeeting REGRETS to: Andrea Patrick, Assistant GFC Secretary, apatrick@ualberta.ca, 780-492-1937 \nPrepared by: Meg Brolley, GFC Secretary and Manager of GFC Operations, 780-492-4733, \nmeg.brolley@ualberta.ca \nUniversity Governance www.governance.ualberta.ca \nhttp://www.governance.ualberta.ca/GeneralFacultiesCouncil/ExecutiveCommittee.aspx\nhttp://www.governance.ualberta.ca/GeneralFacultiesCouncil/NominatingCommittee/Committee-Membership-Replenishment/Current-Vacancies.aspx\nhttp://www.governance.ualberta.ca/GeneralFacultiesCouncil/NominatingCommittee/Committee-Membership-Replenishment/Current-Vacancies.aspx\nhttp://www.uofaweb.ualberta.ca/governance/\n2-24 South Academic Building (SAB)  \nEdmonton, Alberta, Canada  T6G 2G7 \nTel: 780.492.3212 \nwww.president.ualberta.ca  \nOFFICE OF THE PRESIDENT \nDear Members of the General Faculties Council: \nWelcome to the first GFC meeting of 2016! \nAs we turn the calendar to a new year I very much look forward to advancing several initiatives. I am \nenergized by the progress of the Institutional Strategic Plan and am hopeful that members of campus \nwill be able to see themselves reflected in the plan. \nWe have occasionally heard through this consultation process, “why do we need a plan for the whole \nuniversity?” By providing a clear direction, the university’s strategic plan is the single most powerful tool \nfor building a shared vision, enabling co-ordinated efforts, and maximizing finite resources. Our goal is \nto develop a plan that all members of the U of A community create and embrace. It must reflect our \ncommon values and capture our collective vision of what the university aspires to be. In the years \nahead, we will look to this one strategic plan to guide all institutional academic and administrative \npriority-setting, and decision-making.  \nIt was great to see so many GFC members at the joint Board of Governors, GFC, Senate and Alumni \nCouncil Executive retreat on November 23rd. This retreat was the first time that all four of these \nconstituents met around a shared purpose: to identify and understand the critical opportunities and \nchallenges facing the University of Alberta over the next ten years. I look forward to bringing these \ngroups together again to have continued dialogue.  \nI look forward to a robust discussion at this GFC about the mission and values of the university and \nwhether they reflect our current experience and future aspirations. Equally important is the discussion \naround academic governance and how the academic community makes decisions within a collegial \nenvironment.  \nThe coming year will give us some renewal of leadership with several Dean searches set to be \ncompleted in the coming months and with the search for our next Chancellor underway. I encourage all \nmembers of the university community to consider nominating a deserving individual for this key role in \nthe next month.  \nYours sincerely,  \nDavid H. Turpin, CM, LLD, FRSC \nPresident and Vice-Chancellor \nhttp://www.president.ualberta.ca/\n2 \nREPORT OF THE PRESIDENT TO GENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nJANUARY 2016 \nBuilding Community Engagement \nMy focus has been on establishing connections with the university and with our supporters locally, \nprovincially and nationally. Below is a summary of those activities since the last General Faculties \nCouncil meeting: \nInternal Groups \nCampus Forum – Provost and Vice-President (Academic) Steven Dew and I have co-hosted several \nCampus Fora to allow for broad-based engagement throughout the institutional strategic planning \nprocess. Attendees have included, faculty, staff and students, and each Forum has also been \nlivestreamed with over 700 individuals watching online. This consultation is part of a series of \ninstitution-wide events to engage the campus community in the development of the university’s next \ninstitutional strategic plan that have taken place on several campuses.  \nRoundtable Discussions – We held several roundtables with the campus community in the month \nleading to the Holiday Break. These sessions facilitated deeper discussion around many topics and \nbrought to light a number of considerations for the ISP. \nConvocation Ceremonies – It was a privilege to address the convocants who received their degree at \nthe fall ceremonies. I was inspired to see so many bright faces cross the stage and shake their hands \nas they became alumni of the U of A. In addition, the University of Alberta welcomed three more \nhonorary degree recipients into our prestigious group: Hugh Bolton, Her Honour Lois Mitchell and \nSamantha Nutt each received an honorary degree during the fall convocation ceremonies. \nPresident’s Executive Committee – While I meet with this group weekly, we were able spend some \nextra time in January on in-depth discussions around the Institutional Strategic Plan. Our one-day \nretreat focused around a discussion of the feedback we have received thus far. \nExternal Groups \nGovernment – Since my last report I hosted Minister Lori Sigurdson, Minister of Advanced Education \nand Minister of Jobs, Skills, Training and Labour for a tour of North Campus with the team from the \nHealth Sciences Council. This was her first official tour on campus and the morning was a great \nsuccess. \nI have also continued our extensive engagement with government through meetings with MPs Linda \nDuncan and Randy Boissonnault and a visit to Ottawa January 20-22nd to meet with several federal \nofficials. I have also met with provincial deputy ministers.  \nDonors and Industry Supporters – Engaging with key donors and industry partners is a critical aspect of \nmy role and I am pleased with the results of these meetings. Through fostering these relationships, the \nuniversity can realize a variety of positive outcomes. I have travelled recently to Calgary, and Ottawa \nand continue to have strategic meetings in Edmonton, as well.  \n3 \nInitiate Institutional Strategic Planning Process  \nThe undertaking of an Institutional Strategic Plan is among my top priorities at the University of Alberta. \nI am pleased with the progress thus far. We are now coming to the end of the first phase of the \ninstitutional strategic planning process and quickly moving towards the next step: the preparation the \nfirst draft of the plan.  \nWe have convened the Institutional Strategic Planning Advisory Committee, which consists of 21 \nrepresentatives from across U of A’s campuses, faculties, disciplines, student groups, and employee \ncategories. Steve and I have asked them to provide their input and advice throughout the ISP drafting \nprocess. Members of the committee have attended consultation events to listen and learn from the \ncommunity, and they are helping us to assess, interpret, and analyze feedback from the in-person and \nonline feedback to identify emerging themes and draft potential strategies. A list of committee members \ncan be found on the ISP website.  \nSteve and I have held a series of campus forums and roundtable strategic planning discussions. One or \nboth of us have also met directly with the Students’ Union Council, the Students’ Council of Faculty \nAssociations, the Graduate Students’ Association, President’s Advisory Committee of Chairs, GFC’s \nAcademic Planning Committee, Senate Plenary, Indigenous Education Council, Library Council, among \nothers, to consult with them on building the next strategic plan. Additionally we have met with many \ngroups of faculty, staff, and students, as well as members of the Board of Governors, Senate, and \nAlumni Council. In total more than 700 people attended campus consultation events and we have \nreceived more than 100 online and email responses. Members of the ISP Advisory Committee have \nbeen on hand at many public events to listen and hear from the community. \nThe feedback collected through all of these avenues has been as posted online for review by the \nuniversity community. This step allows us to share what we have heard from members of our \ncommunity, and to facilitate a conversation about the process and the outcomes so far. Each set of \nnotes includes a summary page, followed by a complete transcript. We will continue to update this \nrepository as our consultation continues.  \nWe are now working with the ISP Advisory Committee and executive team to identify emerging themes \nand begin the task of drafting specific strategies and goals. We aim to have a first draft available to the \ncampus community by late February or early March, and will continue to elicit feedback through \ncampus forums and online mechanisms as we move forward.  \nAdvancing Specific Priorities \n1) Maskwa House of Learning - Update \nI have received significant and encouraging support for the Maskwa Proposal. Many individuals and \ngroups from the Indigenous community, government and university communities have shown great \ninterest in the project and I am heartened from the support to-date.  \n4 \n2) Scholarship for Syrian Students \nThis award has been offered to two students originally from Syria who have now begun their studies at \nthe University of Alberta. This initiative will continue to search for candidates for the program and assist \ndeserving scholars in need. \nGood News  \nWith the caliber of work being done across our campuses every day we are fortunate at the University \nof Alberta to have many successes I could tell you about. Every day our faculty, operational staff and \nstudents have news-worth accomplishments, each with a history, a future and a team of individuals that \nhelped make it happen. Here is a short update on a few priority projects:  \n1) Maintained relative standing in the Times Higher Education World University Rankings of “most \ninternational universities” – Amongst 13 Canadian universities, the University of Alberta has \nmaintained its position as fourth behind the UBC, McGill and Montreal. All Canadian universities \nthat ranked on this list of top 200 schools from around the world dropped somewhat in absolute \nrank due largely to a change in methodology of the ranking from previous years.  \n2) CAUS team (Financials) – Olds College financials are now being handled by University of \nAlberta. This project has been in the works for several years and the success of this project is \nbased on significant time and effort from the CAUS team. The successful implementation of \nCAUS Financials at Olds College lends to the opportunity and promise to expand this program \nat other institutions. \n3) University of Alberta International (UAI) Share the Cheer – Over the holiday season the \nuniversity community opened their doors to international students who may be far from family or \nmay be unfamiliar with some of the traditions celebrated in Edmonton and Canada. This year \n176 individuals and 6 families were matched with 71 staff, faculty, and alumni hosts. Thank you \nto all those who hosted.  \n4) Mountains 101 – The University of Alberta is set to launch its next Massive Open Online Course \n(MOOC) this coming fall. The U of A’s Canadian Mountain Studies Initiative has struck a \npartnership that will see Parks Canada assist with course content and distribution of promotional \nmaterials. This will be the third in a successful series of U of A MOOCs to date. The timing is \nwonderful if you feel like exploring the Rockies this summer in preparation for the release of the \ncourse as our National Parks will have free entry throughout 2016 in recognition of 150 years \nsince confederation.  \n5 \nAwards: \nCouncil for Advancement and Support of Education (CASE) – The U of A’s Advancement Strategic \nCommunications Team has been honored with 21 awards in District VIII. The awards span all aspects \nof communications — from writing to photography and videography, social media and design.  \nWeston Family Prize for Lifetime Achievement in Northern Research – University of Alberta researcher \nIan Sterling has been awarded a Lifetime Achievement work for his efforts over more than 35 years to \nunderstand the ecology of the Artic and its marine life. His work has led to an new era of understanding \nof the North.  \nDistinguished Service Award for Legal Scholarship - The Law Society of Alberta/Canadian Bar \nAssociation Alberta Branch has awarded Mitchell McInnes, a professor in the Faculty of Law, with a \n2016 Distinguished Service Award in Legal Scholarship. This award is an honour for Mitchell, the \nFaculty of Law and the university and recognizes his prolific scholarly output and impact.  \nItem No. 4 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of January 25, 2016 \nOUTLINE OF ISSUE \nAgenda Title: Institutional Strategic Plan – A discussion on Vision, Mission and Values \nMotion:  N/A \nItem   \nAction Requested Approval Recommendation  Discussion/Advice Information \nProposed by David H. Attachment 1 (pages 1 - 3) Vision, Mission and Values \nOffices of the President and  \nProvost and Vice-President (Academic) \nSouth Academic Building (SAB) \nEdmonton, Alberta, Canada T6G 2G7 \nwww.president.ualberta.ca \nwww.provost.ualberta.ca \nDear Members of General Faculties Council, \nAs we come to the close of the first phase of institutional strategic planning consultations, we would like \nto engage the members of GFC in a discussion of the University of Alberta’s vision, mission, and values \nstatement. Any institution’s vision, mission, and values define its community’s core story and attributes \nand provide a frame for its strategic goals and priorities—the same is true for the University of Alberta. \nOur vision, mission, and values help to answer to two key questions: “who are we?” and “why do we \nundertake the work we do?” As the academic core of the University, GFC is the right body to engage in \nthis discussion. \nAt the January 25th meeting, we would like GFC to consider whether our current vision, mission, and \nvalues statements continue to be appropriate or if updates are needed. For your added consideration, \nwe also include: 1) three core values common to all Canadian universities; and 2) a list of values and \nprinciples that have implicitly and explicitly emerged from the ideas and feedback received during our \nconsultations to date, some of which underline the continued currency of our values, while other \nperhaps push us in new directions.  \nWe look forward to hearing your input and advice on this next Monday. \nDavid H. Turpin     Steven Dew \nPresident and Vice-Chancellor   Provost and Vice-President (Academic) \nAttachments: \nVision, Mission and Values \nPage 2 \nCore values common to Canadian universities \n• Intellectual integrity \n• Freedom of inquiry and expression \n• Equality and dignity of all persons  \nCurrent University of Alberta Vision, Mission, and Values \nVision: \nTo inspire the human spirit through outstanding achievements in learning, discovery, and citizenship in \na creative community, building one of the world’s great universities for the public good. \nMission: \nWithin a vibrant and supportive learning environment, the University of Alberta discovers, disseminates, \nand applies new knowledge through teaching and learning, research and creative activity, community \ninvolvement, and partnerships.  The University of Alberta gives a national and international voice to \ninnovation in our province, taking a lead role in placing Canada at the global forefront. \nValues: \nThe U of A community of students, faculty, staff, and alumni rely on shared, deeply held values that \nguide behaviour and actions. These values are drawn from the principles on which the University of \nAlberta was founded in 1908 and reflect a dynamic, modern institution of higher learning, leading \nchange nationally and internationally. \nExcellence: Excellence in teaching that promotes learning; outstanding research and creative activity \nthat fuel discovery and advance knowledge; and enlightened service that builds citizenship. \nStudent Experience: The centrality of our students and our responsibility to provide an intellectually \nsuperior educational environment. \nIntegrity and Academic Freedom: Integrity, fairness, and principles of ethical conduct built on the \nfoundation of academic freedom, open inquiry, and the pursuit of truth. \nDiversity and Creativity: A diverse, yet inclusive, dynamic collegial community that welcomes change \nand seizes opportunity with passion and creativity. \nPride: Pride in our history and traditions, including contributions from indigenous Aboriginal people and \nother groups, which enrich and distinguish the university. \nPage 3 \nValues emerging from ISP consultation process \nSocial Justice \n• Diversity and inclusivity \n• Equity \n• Fairness \nStewardship \n• Sustainability \n• Stewardship/Service \nExcellence \n• Quality \n• Excellence \nCampus Culture \n• Respect \n• Trust \n• Collaboration and cooperation \n• Leadership and distinction/uniqueness \n• Personal growth \nService \n• Community engagement \n• Public good/ public benefit \n• Transparency \n• Accountability \n• Relevance \nItem No. 5 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nAlignment with Guiding \nDocuments \nInstitutional values (2015 Comprehensive Institutional Plan) \n“Our values: The U of A community of students, faculty, staff, and alumni \nrely on shared, deeply held values that guide behaviour and actions. \nThese values are drawn from the principles on which the University of \nAlberta was founded in 1908 and reflect a dynamic, modern institution of \nhigher learning, leading change nationally and internationally. \nExcellence: Excellence in teaching that promotes learning; outstanding \nresearch and creative activity that fuel discovery and advance \nknowledge; and enlightened service that builds citizenship. \nStudent Experience: The centrality of our students and our responsibility \nto provide an intellectually superior educational environment.  \nIntegrity and Academic Freedom: Integrity, fairness, and principles of \nethical conduct built on the foundation of academic freedom, open \ninquiry, and the pursuit of truth. \nDiversity and Creativity: A diverse, yet inclusive, dynamic collegial \ncommunity that welcomes change and seizes opportunity with passion \nand creativity. \nPride: Pride in our history and traditions, including contributions from \nAboriginal people and other groups, which enrich and distinguish the \nuniversity.” \nItem No. 5 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of January 25, 2016 \nCompliance with Legislation, \nPolicy and/or Procedure \nRelevant to the Proposal \n(please quote legislation and \ninclude identifying section \nnumbers) \n1. Post-Secondary Learning Act (PSLA) \n“Powers of general faculties council \n26(1)Subject to the authority of the board, a general faculties council is \nresponsible for the academic affairs of the university and, without restricting \nthe generality of the foregoing, has the authority to  \n (a) exercise any power of a faculty council that the general faculties council \nconsiders desirable to exercise;  \n (b) consider and make decisions on the reports of the faculty councils as to \nthe programs of study in the faculties;  \n (c) determine all programs of study to which clause (b) does not apply that \nare to be offered by the university for credit toward the requirements for any \ndegree or diploma;  \n (d) determine the timetables for examinations and for lectures and other \ninstruction in each faculty;  \n (e) consider and make decisions on the reports of faculty councils as to the \nappointment of examiners and the conduct and results of examinations in \nthe faculties;  \n (f) provide for the granting and conferring of degrees other than honorary \ndegrees;  \n (g) provide for the preparation and publication of the university calendar;  \n (h) hear and determine appeals from the decisions of faculty  \ncouncils on applications, requests or petitions by students and others;  \n (i) consider all matters reported to it by any faculty council and \ncommunicate its opinion or action on those matters to the faculty council \nconcerned;  \n (j) determine the date for the beginning and end of lectures in the university \nand also the beginning and end of each university term; \n(k) make rules and regulations for the management and operation of \nlibraries;  \n (l) recommend to the board the establishment of faculties, schools, \ndepartments, chairs and programs of study in the university in any subject \nthat the general faculties council thinks fit;  \n (m) make rules and regulations respecting academic awards;  \n (n) determine standards and policies respecting the admission of persons \nto the university as students;  \n (o) make recommendations to the board with respect to affiliation with \nother institutions, academic planning, campus planning, a building program, \nthe budget, the regulation of residences and dining halls, procedures in \nrespect of appointments, promotions, salaries, tenure and dismissals, and \nany other matters considered by the general faculties council to be of \ninterest to the university;  \n (p) authorize lecturing and teaching on the university premises by persons \nother than members of the staff of the university;  \n (q) authorize a school to have a school council of the same nature and with \nthe same powers, duties and functions as a faculty council and, in its \ndiscretion, revoke any authority so given.  \n(2) Any recommendations from the general faculties council to the board \nmust be transmitted to the board through the president. \n(3) A general faculties council may delegate any of its powers, duties and \nfunctions under this Act, including the powers referred to in section 31, as it \nsees fit and may prescribe conditions governing the exercise or \nperformance of any delegated power, duty or function, including the power \nof subdelegation.” \nItem No. 5 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of January 25, 2016 \n2. General Faculties Council Terms of Reference / 3. Mandate \n“Powers Retained by General Faculties Council \nAll powers and responsibilities under Section 26 of the PSLA not \nexpressly delegated now or in the future shall be retained by General \nFaculties Council. (GFC 02 DEC 1966) \nThe issues which remain with GFC or which would be referred by a \nStanding Committee to GFC would generally be in the nature of the \nfollowing: \n• high level strategic and stewardship policy issues or matters of \nsignificant risk to the University; \n• alterations to the mandate, terms of reference, composition, or \nstructure of a Standing Committee; \n• those things which a Standing Committee considers to be of major \nstrategic significance to or long-term impact on the University; \n• those matters on which, in the opinion of a Standing Committee chair, \nthere has been a strong division of opinion within the Standing \nCommittee; and \n• issues in which there is a lack of clarity as to which Standing \nCommittee is responsible. \nPowers of GFC under the PSLA \n• exercise any power of a faculty council that the general faculties \ncouncil considers desirable to exercise; (PSLA Section 26(1)(a)) \n• determine all programs of study to which clause (b) does not apply that \nare to be offered by the university for credit toward the requirements \nfor any degree or diploma; (PSLA Section 26(1)(c)) \n• consider all matters reported to it by any faculty council and \ncommunicate its opinion or action on those matters to the faculty \ncouncil concerned; (PSLA Section 26(1)(i)) \n• make rules and regulations for the management and operation of \nlibraries; (PSLA Section 26(1)(k)) \n• make recommendations to the board with respect to affiliation with \nother institutions, academic planning, campus planning, a building \nprogram, the budget, the regulation of residences and dining halls, \nprocedures in respect of appointments, promotions, salaries, tenure \nand dismissals, and any other matters considered by the general \nfaculties council to be of interest to the university; (GFC 24 NOV 1980) \n(GFC 20 NOV 1995). (PSLA Section 26(1)(o)) [Some aspects of this \nauthority have been delegated to other bodies or Officers and as set \nout in the terms of reference for the appropriate Standing Committees \nof GFC.] \nPowers Under the PSLA as Delegated in Whole or in Part (PSLA \nSection 26(1)) \nSubject to the authority of the board, a general faculties council is \nresponsible for the academic affairs of the university and has delegated \nits authority to \n• consider and make decisions on the reports of the faculty councils as to \nthe programs of study in the faculties; (GFC 30 MAR 1981) (PSLA \nSection 26(1)(b)) \n• determine the timetables for examinations and for lectures and other \ninstruction in each faculty; (PSLA Section 26(1)(d)) \nItem No. 5 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of January 25, 2016 \n• consider and make decisions on the reports of faculty councils as to the \nappointment of examiners and the conduct and results of \nexaminations in the faculties; Delegated in part to Deans with respect to enrolment of \nstudents who constitute a danger or who put the public at risk and to \nthe GFC Practice Review Board (PRB). Delegated in part to \ninstructors with respect to disruptive behavior in class).” \n3. GFC Executive Committee Terms of Reference/3. Mandate of \nthe Committee:  “To act as the executive body of General Faculties \nCouncil and, in general, carry out the functions delegated to it by \nGeneral Faculties Council.” \n[…] \n5. Agendas of General Faculties Council \nItem No. 5 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of January 25, 2016 \nGFC has delegated to the Executive Committee the authority to \ndecide which items are placed on a GFC Agenda, and the order in \nwhich those agenda items appear on each GFC agenda.  \nWhen ordering items, the GFC Executive Committee will be mindful of \nany matters that are of particular concern to students during March \nand April so that the student leaders who bring those items forward \nare able to address these items at GFC before their terms end. (EXEC \n06 NOV 2006)  \n[…] \nWith respect to recommendations from other bodies and other GFC \ncommittees, however, the role of the Executive Committee shall be to \nexamine and debate the substance of reports or recommendations \nand to decide if an item is ready to be forwarded to the full governing \nbody. The Executive Committee may decide to refer a proposal back \nto the originating body, to refer the proposal to another body or \nindividual for study or review, or to take other action in order to ready \na proposal for consideration by General Faculties Council. When the \nGFC Executive Committee forwards a proposal to GFC, it shall make \na recommendation that GFC endorse; endorse with suggested \namendments; not endorse; or forward the proposal with no comment.” \nRouting (Include meeting dates) \nParticipation: \n(parties who have seen the \nproposal and in what capacity) \n• Those who have been \ninformed \n• Those who have been \nconsulted \n• Those who are actively \nparticipating \nWhite Paper on General Faculties Council Reform \n• GFC Executive Committee (for discussion) – April 26, 2013 \n• GFC (for discussion) – June 3, 2013 \nStudents’ Union Discussion Paper on General Faculties Council \n• GFC Executive Committee (for discussion) – March 13, 2014 \nDiscussion Topics for Meetings of General Faculties Council \n(discussion) – GFC Executive Committee: September 8, 2014; \nNovember 12, 2015; January 12, 2015; February 23, 2015 \nGFC Executive Committee (for discussion) - December 7, 2015 \nGFC Executive Committee (for discussion) – January 11, 2016 \nApproval Route (Governance) \n(including meeting dates) \nFinal Approver  \nAttachments  \n1. Attachment 12 ( pages 1 – 8) Minutes of GFC Executive Committee, February 23, 2015 \nPrepared by: Meg Brolley, GFC Secretary and Manager of GFC Services, meg.brolley@ualberta.ca \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nJanuary 25, 2016 \nACADEMIC GOVERNANCE AT THE UNIVERSITY OF ALBERTA \nPurpose: \nTo frame the initial discussion of the revitalization of academic governance and propose next steps \nin the process of considering recent reports and discussion papers on GFC reforms.  \nBackground: \nIn 2013 and 2014, three documents were initiated to consider academic governance: a white \npaper on GFC Reform, a discussion paper on General Faculties Council by the Students’ Union, \nand the Report of the Task Force on GFC Reforms commissioned by the President. The White \nPaper was discussed at GFC Executive in April 2013 and at GFC in June 2013. The SU \nDiscussion Paper was discussed at GFC Executive in March 2014.  \nIn addition, in response to calls for increased discussion at GFC meetings, the GFC Executive \nCommittee developed and discussed guidelines for discussion topics for GFC meetings in \nJanuary/February 2015. \nIn response to a request from the floor at the September 28, 2015 GFC meeting, the Report of the \nTask Force on GFC Reforms was posted online for the information of the community with the \ncommitment of further discussion at GFC on this issue. \nThe GFC Executive Committee reviewed all four documents and associated meeting minutes at \nthe December 7, 2015, and January 11, 2016 meetings in order to frame the discussion for full \nGFC. \nRecommendations made in reports and institutional governance principles: \nMany recommendations were articulated in the SU Discussion Paper and the Report of the Task \nForce, and links to these documents are included. The recommendations made should be \nconsidered in context. Some may continue to resonate, while others, for a variety of reasons, may \nnot.  \nA number of themes arose from these documents: \n• Lack of substantive discussion at GFC \n• Questions regarding delegation \n• Committee structure – role, size, number, membership, overlap, gaps (IT, research), \ninformation flow between committees \n• Slow pace with which proposals go through governance pathways \n• Online records, particularly archives \n Page 2 \nAnother complication with the recommendations is that they are presented at a high level of detail \nwithout asking more foundational questions about the contemporary vision and underlying \nprinciples of governance at the institution. \nFraming a GFC Discussion \nIt is recognized that academic governance is a cornerstone of the University. An effective, \nengaged General Faculties Council and its standing committees is essential to fulfilling the \nresponsibility of GFC. It is clear that subsequent to a re-appraisal of the principles of governance, \nkey issues will be identified and a course of action can be established toward addressing each \nissue. \nThis conversation should start with a high level discussion on the principles that should guide any \nchanges to the current structure that we might want to make. What is the business that full GFC \nshould be discussing and deciding upon? Where does GFC see the balance to be struck between \nlarge policy/strategy issues and more detailed matters? What do you expect of academic \ngovernance? \nThis conversation will hopefully lead to a more detailed set of questions and discussions around \nacademic governance. \nNext Steps  \nIn its mandated role as the executive body of GFC, GFC Executive Committee is willing to facilitate \nmoving the process forward.  \nThe GFC Executive Committee suggests that, after a high level discussion of academic \ngovernance by full GFC and conversation about key issues, the GFC Executive Committee or \nsome other group be tasked to develop concrete plans to prioritize and address the issues in \naccordance with the principles and emphases expressed by full GFC.   \nThe committee is requesting direction and guidance from GFC on how it wishes to proceed.  \nThe following documents and minutes are included with the GFC January 25, 2016 Agenda materials - Item \n5: Academic Governance at the University of Alberta: \n• Academic Governance: Moving Forward - White Paper on General Faculties Sections 26 (1), (2), and (3) of the Post-Secondary Learning Act \n(PSLA) state: \n“Powers of general faculties council \n26(1)Subject to the authority of the board, a general faculties council is \nresponsible for the academic affairs of the university and, without restricting \nthe generality of the foregoing, has the authority to  \n(a) exercise any power of a faculty council that the general faculties council \nconsiders desirable to exercise;  \n(b) consider and make decisions on the reports of the faculty councils as to \nthe programs of study in the faculties;  \n(c) determine all programs of study to which clause (b) does not apply that \nare to be offered by the university for credit toward the requirements for any \ndegree or diploma;  \n(d) determine the timetables for examinations and for lectures and other \ninstruction in each faculty;  \n(e) consider and make decisions on the reports of faculty councils as to the \nappointment of examiners and the conduct and results of examinations in \nthe faculties;  \n(f) provide for the granting and conferring of degrees other than honorary \ndegrees;  \n(g) provide for the preparation and publication of the university calendar;  \n(h) hear and determine appeals from the decisions of faculty  \nItem No. 6 \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of June 3, 2013 \n councils on applications, requests or petitions by students and others;  \n(i) consider all matters reported to it by any faculty council and \ncommunicate its opinion or action on those matters to the faculty council \nconcerned;  \n(j) determine the date for the beginning and end of lectures in the university \nand also the beginning and end of each university term; \n(k) make rules and regulations for the management and operation of \nlibraries;  \n(l) recommend to the board the establishment of faculties, schools, \ndepartments, chairs and programs of study in the university in any subject \nthat the general faculties council thinks fit;  \n(m) make rules and regulations respecting academic awards;  \n(n) determine standards and policies respecting the admission of persons to \nthe university as students;  \n(o) make recommendations to the board with respect to affiliation with other \ninstitutions, academic planning, campus planning, a building program, the \nbudget, the regulation of residences and dining halls, procedures in respect \nof appointments, promotions, salaries, tenure and dismissals, and any other \nmatters considered by the general faculties council to be of interest to the \nuniversity;  \n(p) authorize lecturing and teaching on the university premises by persons \nother than members of the staff of the university;  \n(q) authorize a school to have a school council of the same nature and with \nthe same powers, duties and functions as a faculty council and, in its \ndiscretion, revoke any authority so given.  \n(2) Any recommendations from the general faculties council to the board \nmust be transmitted to the board through the president. \n(3) A general faculties council may delegate any of its powers, duties and \nfunctions under this Act, including the powers referred to in section 31, as it \nsees fit and may prescribe conditions governing the exercise or \nperformance of any delegated power, duty or function, including the power \nof subdelegation.” \n2. White Paper on General Faculties Council Reforms (pages 1 – 3) \nPrepared by: Catherine Swindlehurst, Director, Office of the President, swindlehurst@ualberta.ca  \nmailto:swindlehurst@ualberta.ca\n1 \nDraft White Paper on General Faculties Council Reforms \nOffice of the President \nMay 24, 2013 \nIntroduction \nThe General Faculties Council is integral to the governance and operation of the University of \nAlberta. An effective governance system, particularly within GFC, is imperative to building \nexcellence across the institution. Good governance depends on ensuring the institution has \nrelevant processes and structures to support informed representatives of the University in their \ndecision-making on behalf of the University community. Within GFC and its standing \ncommittees, there are 370 members who provide their time, expertise and service to the \nuniversity community. GFC depends on an engaged community of members working within an \neffective governance system. \nIn order to ensure that our governance system is working effectively, we, as members of this \nsystem, must undertake a periodic review of the structures and processes to ensure that they \nare effective and clearly defined. With significant changes to our institution on the horizon, now \nis the time to ensure that we have the best governance foundation in place to support our \npeople to make the best decisions for the future of the University of Alberta. We have the \nopportunity to revitalize GFC and ensure that the committees are engaged and debating the \ntopics that are the mandate of the GFC, as outlined in the Post-Secondary Learning Act. \nPlan \nIn order to ensure that the GFC system is functioning effectively and efficiently, GFC should \nundertake a review of all of its committees and the overall GFC structure. This process is timely \ngiven the provincial government’s commitment to ensuring effective governance practices \nwithin Alberta’s post-secondary institutions, and compliance with the Public Agencies \nGovernance Framework and the upcoming Alberta Public Agencies Governance Act (APAGA). \nA small task force will be struck by the President, the Chair of GFC, to conduct an independent \nreview of the Terms of Reference and activities of each committee and provide \nrecommendations for reform. In order to maintain its objectivity, the GFC Task Force will \nconsist of two faculty members who have relevant academic and/or professional background \nand expertise in governance. The GFC Secretary will consult with the Task Force in an advisory \ncapacity.  \nAttachment 1\nhttp://www.qp.alberta.ca/1266.cfm?page=p19p5.cfm&leg_type=Acts&isbncln=9780779737932\n2 \nFigure 1: GFC Committee Structure (from Governance 101 presentation) \nThe GFC Task Force will objectively review GFC committees’ structure and activities, and the \nevolution of these, as compared to each committee’s terms of reference, and the PSLA. \nSpecifically, the GFC Task Force will examine: \n1. Each GFC committee’s Terms of Reference to ensure that the terms are up-to-date and \nreflect University policies and the PSLA, but also the current operations of each \ncommittee. \n2. Each committee’s activities to ensure that they are focused on governance issues \nrelevant to that committee, and not activities that are the responsibility of other \ncommittees or administrative offices. \n3. The alignment of the committees to identify duplication and/or gaps in committee \nactivities, as it relates to the governance pathways within GFC committees.  \nIt is imperative that GFC and its committees, University Governance, the Offices of the \nPresident and the Vice-Presidents remain at arms’ length in this process, to ensure that the GFC \nTask Force retains its independence and objectivity in gathering its data and drafting its report \nand recommendations. \nThe GFC Task Force will submit a report of its findings and recommendations to President \nSamarasekera, the Chair of GFC, for review, by the end of August, 2013. The President will \nreview the findings and present the recommendations to the GFC Executive, at its meeting on \nOctober 7, 2013. GFC Executive will consider the recommendations and forward them on to \nGFC for discussion at Council’s October 28th GFC meeting.  \n3 \nTimeline \nIn order to have recommendations approved and ready for implementation in Fall 2013, the \nfollowing timeline is proposed: \n• April 26, 2013 – the GFC Reform White Paper is presented to and discussed by GFC \nExecutive. An implementation plan and process will be decided at this meeting, and \nrecommendations for task force membership. \n• June 3, 2013 – The implementation plan is presented to GFC, and the task force is struck.  \n• August 31, 2013 – Task force report due to the Chair of GFC.  \n• October 7, 2013 – Recommendations presented to GFC Executive for consideration. \n• October 28, 2013 – Recommendations presented to GFC for discussion. \nGeneral Faculties Council  \nExecutive Committee \nApproved Open Session Minutes \nFriday, April 26, 2013 \n2-31 SAB, South Academic Building \n2:00 PM – 4:00 PM \nATTENDEES: \nVoting Members: \nMartin Ferguson-Pell \n(Delegate) \nActing Provost and Vice-President (Academic) and Chair, GFC Executive \nCommittee (delegate) \nColleen Skidmore \n(Delegate) \nVice-Provost and Associate Vice-President (Academic)  \nGerry Kendal Vice-Provost and University Registrar \nDustin Chelen Students’ Union Vice-President (Academic) \nNathan Andrews Graduate Student Association Vice-President (Academic) \nEd Blackburn Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nLise Gotell Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nWendy Rodgers Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nChris de Gara Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nAnita Molzahn Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nDuncan Saunders Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nKaori Kabata Academic Staff, Member of GFC \nAdam Woods Undergraduate Student, Member of GFC \nPresenter(s):  \nMartin Ferguson-Pell Acting Provost and Vice-President (Academic) and Acting Chair, GFC \nExecutive Committee \nIndira Samarasekera President and Chair, General Faculties Council (GFC) \nStaff:  \nGarry Bodnar Director, General Faculties Council (GFC) Services and Secretary to GFC \nMarion Haggarty-France University Secretary \nAndrea Patrick Scribe \nOPENING SESSION \n1.  Approval of the Agenda \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nMotion:  de Gara/Rodgers \nGFC Executive Committee / 4/26/2013 \nPage 2 \nTHAT the GFC Executive Committee approve the Agenda. \nCARRIED \n2. Comments from the Chair and President, General Faculties Council (GFC) \nDr Ferguson-Pell reminded members to check for updates on the Change@Ualberta website regarding the \nimpact of the Provincial Budget and the Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) (previously called the \n“Letter of Expectation”) between the Ministry of Enterprise and Advanced Education (EAE) and the \nUniversity of Alberta. \nDr Ferguson-Pell reported that the tuition increase for the 2013-14 academic year, approved by the Board \nof Governors, was recently disallowed by the Ministry of EAE and that there will be resulting difficulties if \nthe University of Alberta is no longer allowed to increase tuition when necessary. \nHe noted that Faculty-specific budget letters will be forwarded to each Dean shortly. \nDr Ferguson-Pell reported that Central Administration is currently revising the institutional budget, and it will \nbe available for review by the May 22, 2013 GFC Academic Planning Committee (APC) meeting. \nDr Samarasekera briefed members on the meeting between the Ministry of EAE and the 26 Alberta post-\nsecondary presidents held on April 11, 2013.  She noted that the presidents met separately on the morning \nof the meeting and, at that time, items for discussion included the shared sentiment that post-secondary \ninstitutions were blindsided by the funding cuts announced within the Provincial Budget. \nShe stated that the subsequent meeting with the Ministry was a success, citing frankness and openness in \nthe messaging from the presidents to the Ministry.  She reported that those messages related to the \nnegative impact of the budget cuts on Campus Alberta initiatives, issues related to duplication, and the joint \nimpact of receiving sudden, significantly reduced funding as well as losing the ability to increase tuition \nwhen necessary.  She added that the presidents attempted to dispel myths at the meeting.  \nDr Samarasekera noted that further negotiations at the meeting led to the conversion of the Letter of \nExpectation into an MOU format, with additional time to make appropriate revisions extended to \nSeptember, 2013. \nDr Samarasekera reported that the presidents met on April 15, 2013 in Red Deer, and there was \nagreement to create a council of presidents.  She noted that each president will draft a position paper on \ncertain relevant issues including the re-opening of the Post-Secondary Learning Act (PSLA), funding \nframework, tuition, and Campus Alberta. \nDr Samarasekera stated that she continues to push for long-term investment in the University of Alberta.  \nShe explained that the major problems within Alberta’s post-secondary educational landscape relate to \naccess and quality, and that these problems are evidence-based. \nShe reported that Mr Thomas Lukaszuk, Minister of EAE, has offered to continually meet with presidents, \nboard chairs, and students and that she hopes the messaging towards all three groups will be consistent.  \nShe noted that she has a meeting with the Minister next week. \nDr Samarasekera briefed members on the Board of Governors’ Strategic Retreat, held from April 16-19, \n2013.  She stated that the timing of the Retreat was beneficial considering the recent challenges faced by \nthe University of Alberta, however purely coincidental as it was planned approximately one year ago. \nGFC Executive Committee / 4/26/2013 \nPage 3 \nShe reported that the Board of Governors committed unanimously to being one of the best universities in \nthe world and that they requested short- and long-term plans from her, as President.  She stated that the \nRetreat provided clear direction in terms of excellence and reinforced the need to look internally as an \ninstitution into processes and practices that ensure excellence and that a sustainable budget is created \naround excellence, as well. \nDuring the ensuing discussion, members expressed several comments and questions in relation to these \nissues, including, but not limited to:  whether the Deans will have unilateral authority to determine Faculty \ncore cuts; why there was not a request for staff to take a salary cut; clarification about the Ministry’s idea \nthat Campus Alberta equalizes all institutions; that professors are being improperly identified as the source \nof the budget problem at the University of Alberta; and speculation into scenarios next year, in relation to \nfunding. \nDISCUSSION ITEMS \n3. Academic Governance:  Moving Forward \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nPresenter: Indira Samarasekera, President and Chair, General Faculties Council (GFC) \nPurpose of the Discussion:  To engage the GFC Executive Committee and General Faculties Council \n(GFC) in a discussion with regard to the role and responsibilities of GFC and its standing committee \nsystem and to discuss the striking of a task force to review the Terms of Reference and activities of each \nGFC committee and provide recommendations for reform. \nDiscussion: \nDr Samarasekera noted that as President and Chair of General Faculties Council (GFC), she is interested \nin reviewing the GFC Standing Committee Terms of Reference, governance structure, and processes, as \nwell as the general scope of purview for each GFC Standing Committee in relation to administrative issues \nand responsibilities. \nShe noted that, first, there needs to be an effort to introduce debate into GFC, citing the value of large-\nscale, academy-wide discussions surrounding timely and relevant issues such as the re-opening of the \nPost-Secondary Learning Act (PSLA).  She suggested that perhaps such issues could be identified by the \nGFC Executive Committee initially and then placed on each GFC Agenda for debate and deliberation by \nCouncil members.  She added that a significant portion of time at GFC is spent approving routine items. \nShe reported that, secondly, the structure of the GFC Standing Committees contribute to onerous \nduplication of presentations and that there needs to be an effort to streamline the approval process for \nproposals moving through the governance system.  She noted that the private sector utilizes “consent \nagendas” and suggested that this might be an appropriate amendment to current practices at the University \nof Alberta. \nDr Samarasekera stated that, thirdly, there needs to be a review of each individual GFC Standing \nCommittee’s Terms of Reference to ensure that there is a distinction between governance and \nadministration. \nDr Samarasekera reported that her proposal to address these issues includes striking a GFC Task Force, \ncomprised of a small group of governance experts, who will review the current GFC Standing Committee \nGFC Executive Committee / 4/26/2013 \nPage 4 \nand GFC Terms of Reference, as well as their activities, to suggest reforms where necessary to invigorate \nand enrich the scope of the governance environment and ensure that there are effective processes and \npractices in place at a time when changes are imminent at the institution. She added that the group could \nwork over the summer and present its findings and recommendations to full GFC membership at the first \nCouncil meeting in the academic year 2013-2014. \nMr Chelen was invited to present a Students’ Union (SU) proposal, distributed for members’ review, \nentitled, “GFC ad hoc Subcommittee on Collegial Governance, Terms of Reference,” and he explained that \nthe proposal reflects a joint effort between the SU and the Graduate Students’ Association (GSA).   \nIn relation to Dr Samarasekera’s comments, Mr Chelen noted that students have arrived at similar \nconclusions about the governance process and structure, although his proposal suggests a broader task \nforce membership and a timeframe for the project which is longer to allow thorough review and University-\nwide consultation. \nMr Woods stated that GFC should be a forum to discuss and freely debate a large scope of issues and that \nno decisions should be made by a few people privately. \nMr Andrews suggested that students should be represented within the membership of the GFC Task \nForce.  \nDr Samarasekera stated that the purpose of the GFC Task Force is to provide a blueprint of how to take \nadministration out of governance and to review in a clinical fashion the GFC Standing Committees, adding \nthat timely, expert advice is essential in the current financial climate, to prove to the Board of Governors \nthat internal processes remain effective and efficient.  She explained that once this ‘audit’ is completed, \nGFC members will decide how to proceed. \nMs Haggarty-France reported that the last external review of the governance process and structure \noccurred in the early 2000s and that, at one point in the mid 1970s, there were 32 GFC Standing \nCommittees, as opposed to 11 currently.  She stated that the University of Alberta has one of the leanest \nacademic governance committee structures in Canada.  She stated that with the replenishment of the \nAssistant GFC Secretary position in University Governance, there has been increased opportunity to be \nmore strategic and effective.  She stated that it will be beneficial to review governance processes and \npractices and that this may provide further opportunity to educate the community about the different roles \nwithin governance and why each GFC Standing Committee has a distinct and separate mandate. \nDuring the ensuing discussion surrounding this issue, members expressed several comments and \nquestions, including, but not limited to:  clarification about how internal Department-level, Faculty-level, and \nsenior administrative committees add to the perception of a prolonged governance course; the methods \nand outcomes of the last GFC Standing Committee Terms of Reference review; that proposals seem overly \nvetted within the current governance structure; discussion about the proposed timeframe of the GFC Task \nForce; that due to over-exposure during the governance process, proposals and items for discussion seem \n‘fait accompli’ when presented at GFC meetings; that summer might not be the ideal time for the GFC Task \nForce to complete their work; that students should be part of the review process; that perhaps a small \ngroup, viewing things through an administrative lens, could review the GFC Standing Committee Terms of \nReference and then present a report for consultation within the governance structure; that the GFC \nStanding Committees require individual delegated authority to avoid duplication; that trust between the \ngovernance committees is a key issue; that certain GFC Standing Committee functions could be placed on-\nline; that the forum of GFC should include contentious debate, as currently practiced at Students’ Council; \nthat GFC lacks discussion on divisive issues and that Council votes are predictable; clarification about \nGFC Executive Committee / 4/26/2013 \nPage 5 \nwhether the GFC Task Force will be considered Presidential in its origin or rooted within the GFC \nExecutive Committee and/or another entity of the GFC Standing Committee reporting structure and the \nimplications of either entity of origin;  that members of the individual GFC Standing Committees are the \nbest group of experts to review the GFC Standing Committee Terms of Reference;  that though there is \nroom for more enriched discussions at GFC, the main mandate of GFC remains reviewing and/or \napproving items that have been refined through the existing governance processes; that the GFC Terms of \nReference should be reviewed prior to selecting topics for debate and discussion; that institutional support \nof this endeavor will require updates to members over the summer; and that there are too many GFC \nStanding Committees with complex Terms of Reference.    \nDr Samarasekera concluded that the GFC Task Force will be a Presidential task force and that she will \ntherefore begin to recruit members immediately.  She added that the subsequent report will be presented \nat the first GFC Executive Committee meeting of the 2013-2014 academic year.  She instructed members \nto continue to discuss issues that could be added to GFC Agendas for debate and discussion including the \nre-opening of the PSLA and Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) between the Ministry of Enterprise and \nAdvanced Education (EAE) and the University of Alberta, as well as other relevant academy-wide issues. \n4. Question Period \n There were no questions. \nINFORMATION REPORTS \n5. Items Approved by the GFC Executive Committee by E-Mail Ballots \nThere were no items. \n6. Approval of the Agenda \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nDiscussion: \nDr Samarasekera asked that the Agenda be reorganized to accommodate a presenter’s schedule. \nMotion: Belosevic/Amaral \nTHAT the General Faculties Council approve the Agenda, as amended. \nCARRIED \n2. Approval of the Open Session Minutes of March 14, 2013 \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nMotion:  Berger/Lau \nTHAT the General Faculties Council approve the Minutes of March 14, 2013. \nCARRIED \n3. Comments from the President \nPresident and Chair, Dr Indira Samarasekera, welcomed all to the 389th meeting of General Faculties \nCouncil (GFC) and reported:   \n On the retirement of several longstanding GFC members, notably Mr Gerry Kendal, University \nRegistrar, and Mr Ernie Ingles, Vice-Provost and Director, School of Library and Information \nStudies.  She thanked all departing members of GFC for their dedication and hard work. \n On the Provincial Government’s vision of Campus Alberta, the re-opening of the Post-Secondary \nLearning Act (PSLA), and a recent meeting with Mr Thomas Lukaszuk, Deputy Premier and Minister \nof Enterprise and Advanced Education (EAE).  She stated that she will be attempting to gather \nconcrete objectives from the Provincial Government surrounding their plans for Campus Alberta.  \nShe noted that the PSLA serves the University of Alberta well, and it may not be beneficial to re-\nopen it.  At the request of Dr Samarasekera, Acting Provost Dr Ferguson-Pell was invited to \ncomment on a recent meeting he had with Minister Lukaszuk.  He reported that during this meeting, \nthe Minister discussed results-based budgeting, plans for a possible institute that would foster \ncommercialization opportunities across Campus Alberta, potential changes to Alberta Innovates, re-\nGeneral Faculties Council / 6/3/2013 \nPage 4 \nopening the PSLA, and performance criteria for Campus Alberta.  He noted that the discussion did \nnot yield many specific details on these matters. \n On the Memorandum of Understanding (MOU). She reported that following a request from the \nAlberta Council of Presidents, citing the need for the document to be vetted through governance \nprocesses, the Ministry of EAE has agreed to move the deadline for completion of the MOU to \nOctober 31, 2013.  She noted that the University of Alberta will collaborate with fellow \nComprehensive Academic and Research Intensive (CARI) institutions of Alberta in completing \ncertain sections of the MOU and provided members with a governance timeline of a draft MOU \npresentation at the June 21, 2013 Board of Governors meeting, a first draft in July, and then \ndiscussion of the draft MOU at the September 16, 2013 GFC meeting, with an aim to submit a final \ndocument by the stated deadline of October 31, 2013.  She emphasized that the MOU will be a \ncondensed document.  She reminded members to monitor the posts on the University’s Colloquy \nblog for updates. \n On the Worldwide Universities Network (WUN).  She explained to Council that WUN is a group of \n19 research-intensive universities which collaborate on global research topics.  She reported that at \nthe recent WUN meeting, members discussed ideas surrounding the Network’s areas of focus:  \nclimate change, understanding cultures, higher education, and public health.  She noted that food \nsecurity was determined to be the next area of focus and that proposals would be prepared for \nconsideration by several international funding agencies. \nACTION ITEMS \n4. Merger of the Augustana Faculty’s Department of Fine Arts and Department of Humanities \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nPresenter:  Allen Berger, Dean, Augustana Faculty \nPurpose of the Proposal:  To create administrative efficiencies and reduced expenditures and help facilitate \nimproved faculty communication and new collaborations in teaching and research. \nDiscussion: \nDean Berger explained to members that in an attempt to review administrative savings within Augustana \nFaculty, the proposal speaks to the merger of two small departments, resulting in three equally-sized \ndepartments within the Faculty.  He reported that the proposal was approved by Augustana Faculty Council \nunanimously—this serves as a reflection of support from the departments.  He drew members’ attention to \nthe corresponding letters of support for the proposal and noted that programs and courses would not be \nnegatively impacted. \nMotion: Amaral/Molzahn \nTHAT General Faculties Council recommend to the Board of Governors the proposed merger of \nAugustana Faculty’s Department of Fine Arts and Department of Humanities into a single Department of \nFine Arts and Humanities, as submitted by the Dean of Augustana Faculty and as set forth in Attachment \n1, to take effect July 1, 2013.                                                                                                 \n                                                                                                                                                          CARRIED \nGeneral Faculties Council / 6/3/2013 \nPage 7 \nDISCUSSION ITEMS \n6. Academic Governance – Moving Forward \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nPresenter: Indira Samarasekera, President and Chair, GFC \nPurpose of the Discussion: For information. \nDiscussion: \nPresident Samarasekera explained to members that she will be creating an arm’s length GFC Task Force \nto review GFC and its Standing Committees, noting that the review will examine Terms of Reference for \nGFC and each GFC Standing Committee, compare them with the Terms of Reference and activities of \nother GFC Standing Committees, and ensure that there is a clear delineation between governance and \nadministration.  She stated that now is the time to ensure that processes at the University of Alberta are \nstreamlined, effective, and strategic, and she added that GFC should be a forum in which substantive \ndiscussions and debates occur.  She added that she hopes to decrease the level of repetition within the \ngovernance process, ensuring that members’ time is utilized efficiently in an environment when there is a \nneed to do more with fewer resources. \nShe reported that the GFC Task Force will be populated by two faculty members with expertise in \ngovernance as well as one graduate student representative who, similarly, has some expertise in this area.  \nShe stated that a report from the GFC Task Force will be presented to the GFC Executive Committee and \nto GFC in the Fall.  \nDuring the ensuing discussion, members expressed several comments and questions, including, but not \nlimited to:  that it is beneficial to routinely review governance processes for efficiency; clarification on \nwhether the University of Alberta has faculty members with an expertise in university governance; how the \nreview aligns with “Dare to Deliver”; clarification of the scope of the review; that GFC is seen by some to be \na “rubber stamp”; that the GFC Executive Committee retains a lot of power and is seen to be operating \nbeyond GFC; concern that some GFC Standing Committees report to the Board of Governors and, \nseemingly, not GFC; that all GFC Standing Committees should report directly to GFC; that the material on \nthis item, provided to members, did not contain information on the inclusion of the graduate student \nrepresentative on the GFC Task Force; a suggestion to include an undergraduate student representative \non the GFC Task Force; concern that the summer months would not be enough time to complete the \nreview; and clarification about the cross-over between administrative issues and governance. \nAt the conclusion of the discussion, Dr Samarasekera noted she was amenable to this Task Force \nincluding an undergraduate student representative. \n7. The Umbrella Committee (TUC) Report \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nPresenter: Martin Ferguson-Pell, Acting Provost and Vice-President (Academic) \nPurpose of the Discussion: For information. \nDiscussion: \nGeneral Faculties Council / 6/3/2013 \nPage 8 \n Dr Ferguson-Pell explained that ‘The Umbrella Committee (TUC) Report’ represents the final report for \nTUC, adding that the Strategic Initiatives Group (SIG), under the direction of its Chair, Dr Erasmus Okine \n(who was in attendance at this meeting of GFC), will address any remaining topics not considered by TUC \nduring the time in existence. He noted that all other matters are being considered by the Renaissance \nCommittee (REN). \nMembers expressed several comments and questions in relation to this item, including, but not limited to:  \nclarification with regard to the role of REN; and clarification about Central Administration’s plan to address \nthe issue of indirect costs of research. \nACTION ITEM \n8. Budget Principles (and Update) \nMaterials before members are contained in the official meeting file. \nPresenters:  Martin Ferguson-Pell, Acting Provost and Vice-President (Academic); Phyllis Clark, Vice \nPresident (Finance and Administration) \nPurpose of the Proposal:  Section 3(4)(a) of the GFC Academic Planning Committee (APC) Terms of \nReference on budget matters states that GFC APC is to “recommend to GFC on budget principles.” The \nbudget principles as recommended by GFC APC at its meeting of May 22, 2013 are attached for GFC’s \nconsideration. \nDiscussion: \nDr Ferguson-Pell explained to members that in an effort to provide clear guidelines for the University of \nAlberta to direct future academy-wide changes, a set of budget principles had been drafted. \nMembers expressed a number of comments and questions in relation to the budget principles, including, \nbut not limited to:  a suggestion to include the words “publicly funded” within principle 1; clarification about \nthe meaning of “demonstrable excellence”; a suggestion to amend punctuation within the document; that \nCentral Administration may not be able to minimize job losses because certain losses will be directed and \ndecided by individual Faculties; clarification about increasing international student enrolments but not the \nnumber of Canadian students; that Central Administration may have minimal control over increasing the \nnumber and quality of graduate students; clarification about how the costs of new initiatives will be weighed \nagainst the need to maintain existing programs and staff in the current financial climate; clarification about \ncommunicating with frequency and openness in relation to releasing each Faculty’s budget letter publicly; \nwhether Central Administration could release the budget letters to University of Alberta leaders “in \nconfidence”; a suggestion to include an “unintended consequences” clause into the principles; a suggestion \nto include a principle that might address increasing workload and changing working conditions for existing \nstaff; that there could be issues surrounding equity, as a large percentage of full professors are male; \nclarification about the details of determining Faculty-specific differential cuts; that the principles do not \ninclude information about process; clarification about what is being done to prepare for cuts in 2014-2015 \nand 2015-16; clarification about the future impact on tuition rates; and clarification about resource planning \nto ensure that international students maintain their health and wellness while at the University of Alberta. \nMembers discussed suggested revisions and the Mover and Seconder to the Motion before Council agreed \nto several ‘friendly amendments’ to the budget principles. \nMotion: Belosevic/Ingles \nGeneral Faculties Council / 6/3/2013 \nPage 9 \nTHAT General Faculties Council recommend to the Board of Governors the budget principles that will \nguide the University in developing the strategies that will enable the institution to achieve a sustainable \nbudget, as provided by the President’s Executive Committee and as set forth in Attachment 1, as \namended, to take effect upon final approval.                                                                    \n                                                                                                                                                          CARRIED \nDISCUSSION ITEM \n9.
